Habitat varies, see bird notes. 55F, warm, sunny. This is a Desert Ecology Class, Chico State College. We are in the northern end of Ash Meadows in western Nevada. It is a hot, arid land with steep rising mountains which almost totally lack any type of vegetation. Potash Springs, one mile north of Longstreet Springs was where we camped. The springs are an oasis in the desert. Vegetation is very sparse and located primarily around these springs. Plants are Tamarisk, willow, cottonwood,  and some sedges. Away from water the basic shrubs are Mesquite. Some succulents and Creosote present. Buildings at the various sights were built around 1860. Potash Springs is approx. 4 miles west of SR29 and about 10 miles south of Lathrop Wells, NV. Frog Springs and Rodger Springs are located inbetween Potash and Longstreet Springs.----Observers: Myself and Dr. Dempsey----Footnote: 8PM, Lou Davis and I went north 19 miles to some sand dunes. Only insect present were 3 beetles, some grubs and 5 Dune Crickets. These crickets never before found this far north. All beetles proceeding up dunes, none down. When sand was pushed down, beetles always remained on top or ahead of moving sand. 10PM	Potash springs. Lake: Mudflats.

Faint white eye arcs. Dark eyeline, white throat. Blue wing. Separated from a female Garganey by the grayer breast and the eye arcs. Separated the Cinnamon Teal by its warmer coloring than the grayer bird I was looking at. Photo 7353 a bit confusing at first as I was a distance away and the light from the sun was giving me an impression of a white eyebrow and a second eyeline like a Garganey. After 30 minutes of study I was able to figure out that it was a Blue-winged Teal. Leg coloring was deceiving in photo 7353 as the legs looked gray  instead of the yellow legs of a Blue-winged Teal. and a Cinnamon Teal. Leg coloring difficult to distinguish in the field. Only at home was I able to firgure out the leg color.The bird was standing in a muddy area which caused the legs to look gray. By being still I was able to observe the Green-winged Teal, the Blue-winged Teal, the Killdeer and the Least Sandpiper all in one area.
